  \n    Every day, people come to Facebook to share their stories, see the world through the eyes of others, and connect with friends and causes. The conversations that happen on Facebook reflect the diversity of a community of more than two billion people communicating across countries and cultures and in dozens of languages, posting everything from text to photos and videos. \n   We recognize how important it is for Facebook to be a place where people feel empowered to communicate, and we take our role in keeping abuse off our service seriously. That\u2019s why we have developed a set of Community Standards that outline what is and is not allowed on Facebook. Our Standards apply around the world to all types of content. They\u2019re designed to be comprehensive \u2013 for example, content that might not be considered hate speech may still be removed for violating our bullying policies. \n\n     The goal of our Community Standards is to  encourage expression and create a safe environment . We  develop our policies  based on input from our community and from experts in fields such as technology and public safety. Our policies are also rooted in the following principles: \n   \n      \n     Safety:  People need to feel safe in order to build community. We are committed to removing content that encourages real-world harm, including (but not limited to) physical, financial, and emotional injury. \n  \n        \n  \n Voice:  Our mission is all about embracing diverse views. We err on the side of allowing content, even when some find it objectionable, unless removing that content can prevent a specific harm. Moreover, at times we will allow content that might otherwise violate our standards if we feel that it is newsworthy, significant, or important to the public interest. We do this only after weighing the public interest value of the content against the risk of real-world harm. \n  \n    \n      \n Equity:  Our community is global and diverse. Our policies may seem broad, but that is because we apply them consistently and fairly to a community that transcends regions, cultures, and languages. As a result, our Community Standards can sometimes appear less nuanced than we would like, leading to an outcome that is at odds with their underlying purpose. For that reason, in some cases, and when we are provided with additional context, we make a decision based on the spirit, rather than the letter, of the policy.\n \n\n    \n     Everyone on Facebook plays a part in keeping the platform safe and respectful. We ask people to share responsibly and to let us know when they see something that may violate our Community Standards. We make it easy for people to report potentially violating content, including Pages, Groups, profiles, individual content, and\/or comments to us for review. We also give people the option to  block ,  unfollow , or  hide  people and posts, so that they can control their own experience on Facebook. \n\n     The consequences for violating our Community Standards vary depending on the severity of the violation and a person's history on the platform. For instance, we may warn someone for a first violation, but if they continue to violate our policies, we may restrict their ability to post on Facebook or disable their profile. We also may notify law enforcement when we believe there is a genuine risk of physical harm or a direct threat to public safety.  \n\n     Our Community Standards, which we will continue to develop over time, serve as a guide for how to communicate on Facebook. It is in this spirit that we ask members of the Facebook community to follow these guidelines. \n    \n ","policy_rationale":null},"cruel_insensitive":{"other_content":null,"policy_rationale":null},"spam":{"other_content":null,"policy_rationale":null},"misrepresentation":{"other_content":null,"policy_rationale":null},"false_news":{"other_content":null,"policy_rationale":null},"memorialization":{"other_content":null,"policy_rationale":null},"intellectual_property":{"other_content":null,"policy_rationale":null},"user_requests":{"other_content":null,"policy_rationale":null},"additional_protection_minors":{"other_content":null,"policy_rationale":null},"stakeholder_engagement":{"other_content":null,"policy_rationale":null}},"rawIntroContent":"\n   \n     Every day, people come to Facebook to be heard and to hear others, by sharing their stories, connecting with friends and family, and building communities. We are a home for more than two billion people to express themselves and share their experiences across countries and cultures and in dozens of languages. \n     We recognize how important it is for Facebook to be a place where people feel empowered to communicate, and we take seriously our role in keeping abuse off our service . That\u2019s why we have developed a set of Community Standards that outline what is and is not allowed on Facebook. Our policies are based on feedback from our community and the advice of experts in fields such as technology, public safety and international human rights. To ensure that everyone\u2019s voice is valued, we take great care to craft policies that are inclusive of different views and beliefs, in particular those of people and communities that might otherwise be overlooked or marginalized. \n     EXPRESSION \n     The goal of our Community Standards is foremost to create a place for   expression and give people voice. Our mission to build community and bring the world closer together depends on people\u2019s ability to share diverse views, experiences, ideas, and information. We want people to be able to talk openly about the issues that matter to them, even if some people may find it disagreeable or objectionable. We may even allow content that would otherwise go against our Community Standards if it is newsworthy or in the public interest. We do this only after weighing the public interest value against the risk of harm and and we look to international human rights standards to make these judgments.   \n    \n     Our commitment to expression is paramount, but we recognize that the internet is unique in that it creates new and increased opportunities for abuse. That\u2019s why when we limit expression, we do so in service of one or more the following values: \n   \n      \n    \n     Safety:  We are committed to making Facebook a safe place. Expression that threatens people has the potential to intimidate, exclude or silence others and isn\u2019t allowed on Facebook. \n  \n        \n  \n    \n     Dignity: We believe that all people are equal in dignity and rights. We expect that people will respect the dignity of others and not harass or degrade people. \n  \n    \n      \n    \n    \n     Privacy:  We are committed to protecting personal privacy and information. Privacy gives people the freedom to be themselves, to choose how and when to share on Facebook and to connect more easily.\n \n   \n       Authenticity:  We want to help make sure the content people are seeing on Facebook is authentic. We believe that authenticity creates a better environment for sharing, and that\u2019s why we don\u2019t want people using Facebook to misrepresent who they are or what they\u2019re doing.\n \n    \n    \n     Our Community Standards apply to everyone, all around the world, and to all types of content. They\u2019re designed to be comprehensive \u2013 for example, content reported as hate speech may not fall within that policy but may still be removed for violating a different policy. We recognize that words may mean different things or affect people differently depending on their local community, language, or background. We work hard to account for these nuances while also seeking to apply our policies consistently and fairly to people and their expression. \n\n     People can let us know if they come across potentially violating content, including Pages, Groups, profiles, individual content, and comments, by reporting it to us. We also give people control over their own experience on Facebook by allowing them to \n       block\n       \n    ,\n        unfollow\n       \n       or \n        hide\n        \n       people and posts.\n       \n\n     The consequences for violating our Community Standards vary depending on the severity of the violation and the person's history on the platform. For instance, we may warn someone for a first violation, but if they continue to violate our policies, we may restrict their ability to use certain Facebook features or disable their profile. We also may notify law enforcement when we believe there is a genuine risk of physical harm or a direct threat to public safety. \n     Our Community Standards are a guide for how to communicate on Facebook. It is in this spirit that we ask members of the Facebook community to follow these guidelines. \n    \n
